<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg/150px-Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg" width="150" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg/225px-Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg/300px-Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4288" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The urban poor buy water from water vendors for, on average, about five to 16 times the metered price.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenny_130-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenny-130">[129]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Similarly, the poorest fifth receive 0.1% of the world’s lighting but pay a fifth of total spending on light, accounting for 25 to 30 percent of their income.<sup id="cite_ref-solar_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solar-134">[133]</a></sup> Indoor air pollution from burning fuels kills 2 million, with almost half the deaths from pneumonia in children under 5.<sup id="cite_ref-bamboo_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bamboo-135">[134]</a></sup> Fuel from Bamboo burns more cleanly and also matures much faster than wood, thus also reducing deforestation.<sup id="cite_ref-bamboo_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bamboo-135">[134]</a></sup> Additionally, using solar panels is promoted as being cheaper over the products' lifetime even if upfront costs are higher.<sup id="cite_ref-solar_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solar-134">[133]</a></sup> Thus, payment schemes such as lend-to-own programs are promoted and up to 14% of <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenyan</a> households use solar as their primary energy source.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Violence">Violence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Violence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">Slavery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">Human trafficking</a></div>
<p>According to experts, many women become victims of trafficking, the most common form of which is <a href="/wiki/Survival_sex" title="Survival sex">prostitution</a>, as a means of survival and economic desperation.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> Deterioration of living conditions can often compel children to abandon school to contribute to the family income, putting them at risk of being exploited.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> For example, in <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>, a number of girls are turning to sex in return for food to survive because of the increasing poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> According to studies, as poverty decreases there will be fewer and fewer instances of violence.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>In one survey, 67% of children from disadvantaged <a href="/wiki/Inner_city" title="Inner city">inner cities</a> said they had witnessed a serious assault, and 33% reported witnessing a homicide.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> 51% of fifth graders from <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> (median income for a household: $27,133) have been found to be victims of violence, compared to 32% in Washington, DC (mean income for a household: $40,127).<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personality">Personality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Personality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Max_Weber" title="Max Weber">Max Weber</a> and some schools of <a href="/wiki/Modernization_theory" title="Modernization theory">modernization theory</a> suggest that cultural <a href="/wiki/Value_(personal_and_cultural)" class="mw-redirect" title="Value (personal and cultural)">values</a> could affect economic success.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> However, researchers<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (November 2009)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> have gathered evidence that suggest that values are not as deeply ingrained and that changing economic opportunities explain most of the movement into and out of poverty, as opposed to shifts in values.<sup id="cite_ref-kerbo2006a_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kerbo2006a-145">[144]</a></sup> Studies have shown that poverty changes the personalities of children who live in it. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Smoky_Mountains_Study" title="Great Smoky Mountains Study">Great Smoky Mountains Study</a> was a ten-year study that was unexpectedly able to demonstrate this. During the study, about one-quarter of the families saw a dramatic and unexpected increase in income. The study showed that among these children, instances of behavioral and emotional disorders decreased, and conscientiousness and agreeableness increased.<sup id="cite_ref-MyUser_The_Washington_Post_October_8_2015c_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MyUser_The_Washington_Post_October_8_2015c-146">[145]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bettler_peking1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Bettler_peking1.jpg/220px-Bettler_peking1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Bettler_peking1.jpg/330px-Bettler_peking1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Bettler_peking1.jpg/440px-Bettler_peking1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1532" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bettler_peking1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A beggar in the streets of Beijing, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> in 2005. Disability discrimination is a major cause of extreme poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-disabpov_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-disabpov-147">[146]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discrimination">Discrimination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Discrimination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cultural factors, such as discrimination of various kinds, can negatively affect productivity such as <a href="/wiki/Ageism" title="Ageism">age discrimination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stereotype" title="Stereotype">stereotyping</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> discrimination against people with physical disability,<sup id="cite_ref-disabpov_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-disabpov-147">[146]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">gender discrimination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racial discrimination</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Caste" title="Caste">caste discrimination</a>. Women are the group suffering from the highest rate of poverty after children; 14.5% of women and <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_the_United_States#Poverty_and_age" title="Poverty in the United States">22% of children are poor in the United States</a>. In addition, the fact that women are more likely to be caregivers, regardless of income level, to either the generations before or after them, exacerbates the burdens of their poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Poverty_reduction">Poverty reduction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Poverty reduction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Poverty_reduction" title="Poverty reduction">Poverty reduction</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Aid" title="Aid">Aid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Development_aid" title="Development aid">Development aid</a></div>
<p>Various poverty reduction strategies are broadly categorized here based on whether they make more of the basic human needs available or whether they increase the <a href="/wiki/Disposable_income" class="mw-redirect" title="Disposable income">disposable income</a> needed to purchase those needs. Some strategies such as building roads can both bring access to various basic needs, such as fertilizer or healthcare from urban areas, as well as increase incomes, by bringing better access to urban markets.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Increasing_the_supply_of_basic_needs">Increasing the supply of basic needs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Increasing the supply of basic needs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_other_goods">Food and other goods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Food and other goods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kunstmestpendelstrooier.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Kunstmestpendelstrooier.jpg/220px-Kunstmestpendelstrooier.jpg" width="220" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Kunstmestpendelstrooier.jpg/330px-Kunstmestpendelstrooier.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Kunstmestpendelstrooier.jpg/440px-Kunstmestpendelstrooier.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1267" data-file-height="1121" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kunstmestpendelstrooier.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A large, modern fertilizer spreader</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Agricultural technologies such as <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_fertilizer" class="mw-redirect" title="Nitrogen fertilizer">nitrogen fertilizers</a>, pesticides, new seed varieties and new irrigation methods have dramatically reduced food shortages in modern times by boosting yields past previous constraints.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, poverty had been mostly accepted as inevitable as economies produced little, making wealth scarce.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-151">[150]</a></sup> Geoffrey Parker wrote that "In <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a>, two of the largest cities in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">western Europe</a>, by 1600 three-quarters of the total population were too poor to pay taxes, and therefore likely to need relief in times of crisis."<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup> The initial industrial revolution led to high economic growth and eliminated mass absolute poverty in what is now considered the developed world.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-153">[152]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">Mass production</a> of goods in places such as rapidly industrializing China has made what were once considered luxuries, such as vehicles and computers, inexpensive and thus accessible to many who were otherwise too poor to afford them.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>Even with new products, such as better seeds, or greater volumes of them, such as industrial production, the poor still require access to these products. Improving <a href="/wiki/Road" title="Road">road</a> and transportation infrastructure helps solve this major bottleneck. In Africa, it costs more to move fertilizer from an African seaport 60 miles inland than to ship it from the United States to Africa because of sparse, low-quality roads, leading to fertilizer costs two to six times the world average.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Microfranchising" title="Microfranchising">Microfranchising</a> models such as door to door distributors who earn commission-based income or <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>'s successful distribution system<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> are used to disseminate basic needs to remote areas for below market prices.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-microfranchising_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-microfranchising-160">[159]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care_and_education">Health care and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Health care and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg/220px-Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg/330px-Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg/440px-Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hardwood surgical tables are commonplace in rural <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigerian</a> clinics.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Health_care_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Health care system">Health care system</a> and <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">Primary education</a></div>
<p>Nations do not necessarily need wealth to gain health.<sup id="cite_ref-Disease_Control_Priorities_Project_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Disease_Control_Priorities_Project-161">[160]</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> had a <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternal mortality rate">maternal mortality rate</a> of 2% in the 1930s, higher than any nation today.<sup id="cite_ref-post_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post-162">[161]</a></sup> It reduced it to 0.5–0.6% in the 1950s and to 0.6% today while spending less each year on <a href="/wiki/Maternal_health" title="Maternal health">maternal health</a> because it learned what worked and what did not.<sup id="cite_ref-post_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post-162">[161]</a></sup> Knowledge on the cost effectiveness of healthcare interventions can be elusive and educational measures have been made to disseminate what works, such as the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Consensus" title="Copenhagen Consensus">Copenhagen Consensus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> Cheap <a href="/wiki/Water_filter" title="Water filter">water filters</a> and promoting hand washing are some of the most cost effective health interventions and can cut <a href="/wiki/Child_mortality" title="Child mortality">deaths</a> from <a href="/wiki/Diarrhea" title="Diarrhea">diarrhea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>Strategies to provide education cost effectively include <a href="/wiki/Deworming" title="Deworming">deworming</a> children, which costs about 50 cents per child per year and reduces non-attendance from <a href="/wiki/Anemia" title="Anemia">anemia</a>, illness and malnutrition, while being only a twenty-fifth as expensive as increasing school attendance by constructing schools.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup> Schoolgirl absenteeism could be cut in half by simply providing free <a href="/wiki/Sanitary_towel" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanitary towel">sanitary towels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Food_fortification" title="Food fortification">Fortification</a> with <a href="/wiki/Micronutrient" title="Micronutrient">micronutrients</a> was ranked the most cost effective aid strategy by the Copenhagen Consensus.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Iodised_salt" title="Iodised salt">iodised salt</a> costs 2 to 3 cents per person a year while even moderate <a href="/wiki/Iodine_deficiency" title="Iodine deficiency">iodine deficiency</a> in pregnancy shaves off 10 to 15 <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_quotient" title="Intelligence quotient">IQ</a> points.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup> Paying for school meals is argued to be an efficient strategy in increasing school enrollment, reducing absenteeism and increasing student attention.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup></p>
<p>Desirable actions such as enrolling children in school or receiving vaccinations can be encouraged by a form of aid known as <a href="/wiki/Conditional_cash_transfer" title="Conditional cash transfer">conditional cash transfers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brazil_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brazil-171">[170]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, for example, dropout rates of 16- to 19-year-olds in rural area dropped by 20% and children gained half an inch in height.<sup id="cite_ref-csm_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csm-172">[171]</a></sup> Initial fears that the program would encourage families to stay at home rather than work to collect benefits have proven to be unfounded. Instead, there is less excuse for neglectful behavior as, for example, children stopped begging on the streets instead of going to school because it could result in suspension from the program.<sup id="cite_ref-csm_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csm-172">[171]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Removing_constraints_on_government_services">Removing constraints on government services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Removing constraints on government services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Political_corruption" title="Political corruption">Political corruption</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tax_havens" class="mw-redirect" title="Tax havens">Tax havens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transfer_mispricing" title="Transfer mispricing">Transfer mispricing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Developing_countries%27_debt" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing countries' debt">Developing countries' debt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Conditionality" title="Conditionality">Conditionality</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Waiting_for_goods.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Waiting_for_goods.JPG/220px-Waiting_for_goods.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Waiting_for_goods.JPG/330px-Waiting_for_goods.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Waiting_for_goods.JPG/440px-Waiting_for_goods.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Waiting_for_goods.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Local citizens from the Jana bi Village wait their turn to gather goods from the Sons of Iraq (Abna al-Iraq) in a military operation conducted in Yusufiyah, Iraq.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Government revenue can be diverted away from basic services by corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-unodc_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unodc-173">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> Funds from aid and natural resources are often sent by government individuals for <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a> to overseas banks which insist on <a href="/wiki/Bank_secrecy" title="Bank secrecy">bank secrecy</a>, instead of spending on the poor.<sup id="cite_ref-graft_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-graft-175">[174]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Global_Witness" title="Global Witness">Global Witness</a> report asked for more action from Western banks as they have proved capable of stanching the flow of funds linked to terrorism.<sup id="cite_ref-graft_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-graft-175">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Illicit_financial_flows" title="Illicit financial flows">Illicit capital flight</a> from the developing world is estimated at ten times the size of aid it receives and twice the debt service it pays,<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> with one estimate that most of Africa would be developed if the taxes owed were paid.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup> About 60 per cent of illicit capital flight from Africa is from <a href="/wiki/Transfer_mispricing" title="Transfer mispricing">transfer mispricing</a>, where a <a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">subsidiary</a> in a developing nation sells to another subsidiary or <a href="/wiki/Shell_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Shell company">shell company</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a> at an artificially low price to pay less tax.<sup id="cite_ref-transparency_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transparency-178">[177]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> report estimates that about 30% of sub-Saharan Africa's GDP has been moved to <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax havens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-179">[178]</a></sup> Solutions include corporate "country-by-country reporting" where corporations disclose activities in each country and thereby prohibit the use of tax havens where no effective economic activity occurs.<sup id="cite_ref-transparency_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transparency-178">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Developing_countries%27_debt" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing countries' debt">Developing countries' debt service</a> to banks and governments from richer countries can constrain government spending on the poor.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> spent 40% of its total budget to repay foreign debt, and only 7% for basic state services in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-worldcentric.org_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldcentric.org-181">[180]</a></sup> One of the proposed ways to help poor countries has been <a href="/wiki/Debt_relief" title="Debt relief">debt relief</a>. Zambia began offering services, such as free health care even while overwhelming the health care infrastructure, because of savings that resulted from a 2005 round of <a href="/wiki/Debt_relief" title="Debt relief">debt relief</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, as primary holders of developing countries' debt, attach <a href="/wiki/Structural_adjustment" title="Structural adjustment">structural adjustment</a> <a href="/wiki/Conditionality" title="Conditionality">conditionalities</a> in return for loans which are generally geared toward loan repayment with <a href="/wiki/Austerity" title="Austerity">austerity</a> measures such as the elimination of state subsidies and the privatization of state services. For example, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> presses poor nations to eliminate subsidies for fertilizer even while many farmers cannot afford them at market prices.<sup id="cite_ref-Malawi_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Malawi-183">[182]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a>, almost five million of its 13 million people used to need emergency food aid but after the government changed policy and subsidies for fertilizer and seed were introduced, farmers produced record-breaking corn harvests in 2006 and 2007 as Malawi became a major food exporter.<sup id="cite_ref-Malawi_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Malawi-183">[182]</a></sup> A major proportion of aid from donor nations is <a href="/wiki/Tied_aid" title="Tied aid">tied</a>, mandating that a receiving nation spend on products and expertise originating only from the donor country.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup> US law requires <a href="/wiki/Food_aid" class="mw-redirect" title="Food aid">food aid</a> be spent on buying food at home, instead of where the hungry live, and, as a result, half of what is spent is used on transport.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Distressed_securities_fund" class="mw-redirect" title="Distressed securities fund">Distressed securities funds</a>, also known as <i>vulture funds</i>, buy up the debt of poor nations cheaply and then sue countries for the full value of the debt plus interest which can be ten or 100 times what they paid.<sup id="cite_ref-vulture_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vulture-186">[185]</a></sup> They may pursue any companies which do business with their target country to force them to pay to the fund instead.<sup id="cite_ref-vulture_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vulture-186">[185]</a></sup> Considerable resources are diverted on costly court cases. For example, a court in <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a> ordered <a href="/wiki/The_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="The Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congo</a> to pay an American speculator $100 million in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-vulture_186-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vulture-186">[185]</a></sup> Now, the <a href="/wiki/UK" class="mw-redirect" title="UK">UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> and Jersey have banned such payments.<sup id="cite_ref-vulture_186-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vulture-186">[185]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_(bad_effects).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_%28bad_effects%29.jpg/220px-Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_%28bad_effects%29.jpg" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_%28bad_effects%29.jpg/330px-Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_%28bad_effects%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_%28bad_effects%29.jpg/440px-Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_%28bad_effects%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2780" data-file-height="2276" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_(bad_effects).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a> placard in <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>. It shows some negative effects of having too many children.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reversing_brain_drain">Reversing brain drain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Reversing brain drain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Reverse_brain_drain" title="Reverse brain drain">Reverse brain drain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_capital_flight" title="Human capital flight">Human capital flight</a></div>
<p>The loss of basic needs providers emigrating from impoverished countries has a damaging effect.<sup id="cite_ref-Philippines_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philippines-187">[186]</a></sup> As of 2004, there were more Ethiopia-trained doctors living in Chicago than in Ethiopia.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[187]</a></sup> Proposals to mitigate the problem include compulsory government service for graduates of public medical and nursing schools<sup id="cite_ref-Philippines_187-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philippines-187">[186]</a></sup> and promoting <a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">medical tourism</a> so that health care personal have more incentive to practice in their home countries.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Controlling_overpopulation">Controlling overpopulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Controlling overpopulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_overpopulation" title="Human overpopulation">Human overpopulation</a></div>
<p>Some argue that overpopulation and lack of access to birth control leads to population increase to exceed food production and other resources.<sup id="cite_ref-birthrates_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-birthrates-44">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup> Better education for both men and women, and more control of their lives, reduces population growth due to <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-empower_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-empower-192">[191]</a></sup> According to UNFPA-United Nations Population Fund, by giving better education to men and women, they can earn money for their lives and can help them to strengthen economic security.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Increasing_personal_income">Increasing personal income</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Increasing personal income">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following are strategies used or proposed to increase personal incomes among the poor. Raising farm incomes is described as the core of the antipoverty effort as three-quarters of the poor today are farmers.<sup id="cite_ref-agriculture_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agriculture-194">[193]</a></sup> Estimates show that growth in the agricultural productivity of small farmers is, on average, at least twice as effective in benefiting the poorest half of a country’s population as growth generated in nonagricultural sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Income_grants">Income grants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Income grants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Afghan_girl_begging.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Afghan_girl_begging.jpg/220px-Afghan_girl_begging.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Afghan_girl_begging.jpg/330px-Afghan_girl_begging.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Afghan_girl_begging.jpg/440px-Afghan_girl_begging.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="867" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Afghan_girl_begging.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Afghan girl begging in <a href="/wiki/Kabul" title="Kabul">Kabul</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Guaranteed_minimum_income" title="Guaranteed minimum income">Guaranteed minimum income</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_security" title="Social security">Social security</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Welfare" title="Welfare">Welfare</a></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Guaranteed_minimum_income" title="Guaranteed minimum income">guaranteed minimum income</a> ensures that every citizen will be able to purchase a desired level of basic needs. A <a href="/wiki/Basic_income" title="Basic income">basic income</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Negative_income_tax" title="Negative income tax">negative income tax</a>) is a system of <a href="/wiki/Social_security" title="Social security">social security</a>, that periodically provides each citizen, rich or poor, with a sum of money that is <a href="/wiki/Sufficient" class="mw-redirect" title="Sufficient">sufficient</a> to live on. Studies of large cash-transfer programs in Ethiopia, Kenya, and Malawi show that the programs can be effective in increasing consumption, schooling, and nutrition, whether they are tied to such conditions or not.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Spiegel_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spiegel-197">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Namibians_line_up_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Namibians_line_up-198">[197]</a></sup> Proponents argue that a basic income is more economically efficient than a <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unemployment_benefit" class="mw-redirect" title="Unemployment benefit">unemployment benefits</a>, as the minimum wage effectively imposes a high marginal tax on employers, causing <a href="/wiki/Deadweight_loss" title="Deadweight loss">losses in efficiency</a>. In 1968, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Samuelson" title="Paul Samuelson">Paul Samuelson</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Kenneth_Galbraith" title="John Kenneth Galbraith">John Kenneth Galbraith</a> and another 1,200 economists signed a document calling for the US Congress to introduce a system of income guarantees.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup> Winners of the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize in Economics">Nobel Prize in Economics</a>, with often diverse political convictions, who support a basic income include <a href="/wiki/Herbert_A._Simon" title="Herbert A. Simon">Herbert A. Simon</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Standing_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Standing-200">[199]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Hayek" title="Friedrich Hayek">Friedrich Hayek</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[200]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Solow" title="Robert Solow">Robert Solow</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Standing_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Standing-200">[199]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Milton_Friedman" title="Milton Friedman">Milton Friedman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[201]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jan_Tinbergen" title="Jan Tinbergen">Jan Tinbergen</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Standing_200-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Standing-200">[199]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Tobin" title="James Tobin">James Tobin</a><sup id="cite_ref-Steensland_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steensland-203">[202]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[203]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[204]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/James_Meade" title="James Meade">James Meade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Standing_200-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Standing-200">[199]</a></sup></p>
<p>Income grants are argued to be vastly more efficient in extending basic needs to the poor than <a href="/wiki/Subsidies" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsidies">subsidizing</a> supplies whose effectiveness in poverty alleviation is diluted by the non-poor who enjoy the same subsidized prices.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[205]</a></sup> With cars and other appliances, the wealthiest 20% of Egypt uses about 93% of the country's fuel subsidies.<sup id="cite_ref-fossilfuel_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fossilfuel-207">[206]</a></sup> In some countries, fuel subsidies are a larger part of the budget than health and education.<sup id="cite_ref-fossilfuel_207-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fossilfuel-207">[206]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[207]</a></sup> A 2008 study concluded that the money spent on in-kind transfers in India in a year could lift all India’s poor out of poverty for that year if transferred directly.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[208]</a></sup> The primary obstacle argued against direct cash transfers is the impractically for poor countries of such large and direct transfers. In practice, payments determined by complex iris scanning are used by war-torn <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[209]</a></sup> while India is phasing out its fuel subsidies in favor of direct transfers.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[210]</a></sup> Additionally, in aid models, the <a href="/wiki/Famine_relief" title="Famine relief">famine relief</a> model increasingly used by aid groups calls for giving cash or cash vouchers to the hungry to pay local farmers instead of buying food from donor countries, often required by law, as it wastes money on transport costs.<sup id="cite_ref-csmonitor_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csmonitor-212">[211]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wfp_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wfp-213">[212]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_freedoms">Economic freedoms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Economic freedoms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Economic_freedom" title="Economic freedom">Economic freedom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red_tape" title="Red tape">Red tape</a></div>
<p>Corruption often leads to many <a href="/wiki/Civil_service" title="Civil service">civil services</a> being treated by governments as employment agencies to loyal supporters<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup> and so it could mean going through 20 procedures, paying $2,696 in fees and waiting 82 business days to start a business, in Bolivia, while, in Canada, it takes two days, two registration procedures, and $280 to do the same.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup> Such costly barriers favor big firms at the expense of small enterprises, where most jobs are created.<sup id="cite_ref-cato_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cato-216">[215]</a></sup> Often, businesses have to bribe government officials even for routine activities, which is, in effect, a tax on business.<sup id="cite_ref-macroeconomics1_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-macroeconomics1-217">[216]</a></sup> Noted reductions in poverty in recent decades has occurred in China and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> mostly as a result of the abandonment of <a href="/wiki/Collective_farming" title="Collective farming">collective farming</a> in China and the ending of the <a href="/wiki/Central_planning" class="mw-redirect" title="Central planning">central planning</a> model known as the <a href="/wiki/License_Raj" class="mw-redirect" title="License Raj">License Raj</a> in India.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc1_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-218">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[218]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[219]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> concludes that governments and feudal elites extending to the poor the right to the land that they live and use are 'the key to reducing poverty' citing that land rights greatly increase poor people's wealth, in some cases doubling it.<sup id="cite_ref-landrights_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-landrights-221">[220]</a></sup> Although approaches varied, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> said the key issues were security of tenure and ensuring land transactions costs were low.<sup id="cite_ref-landrights_221-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-landrights-221">[220]</a></sup></p>
<p>Greater access to markets brings more income to the poor. <a href="/wiki/Road" title="Road">Road</a> infrastructure has a direct impact on poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-GCR_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCR-222">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[222]</a></sup> Additionally, migration from poorer countries resulted in $328 billion sent from richer to poorer countries in 2010, more than double the $120 billion in official aid flows from <a href="/wiki/OECD" class="mw-redirect" title="OECD">OECD</a> members. In 2011, India got $52 billion from its <a href="/wiki/Diaspora" title="Diaspora">diaspora</a>, more than it took in <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[223]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_services">Financial services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Financial services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg/220px-Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg/330px-Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg/440px-Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="876" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Information_and_communication_technologies_for_development" title="Information and communication technologies for development">Information and communication technologies for development</a> help to fight poverty.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Microfinance" title="Microfinance">Microfinance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microcredit" title="Microcredit">Microcredit</a></div>
<p>Microloans, made famous by the <a href="/wiki/Grameen_Bank" title="Grameen Bank">Grameen Bank</a>, is where small amounts of money are loaned to farmers or villages, mostly women, who can then obtain physical capital to increase their economic rewards. However, microlending has been criticized for making hyperprofits off the poor even from its founder, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Yunus" title="Muhammad Yunus">Muhammad Yunus</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[224]</a></sup> and in India, <a href="/wiki/Arundhati_Roy" title="Arundhati Roy">Arundhati Roy</a> asserts that some 250,000 debt-ridden farmers have been driven to suicide.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[225]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[226]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[227]</a></sup></p>
<p>Those in poverty place overwhelming importance on having a safe place to save money, much more so than receiving loans.<sup id="cite_ref-time.com_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time.com-229">[228]</a></sup> Additionally, a large part of <a href="/wiki/Microfinance" title="Microfinance">microfinance</a> loans are spent not on investments but on products that would usually be paid by a <a href="/wiki/Checking_account" class="mw-redirect" title="Checking account">checking</a> or <a href="/wiki/Savings_account" title="Savings account">savings account</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-time.com_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time.com-229">[228]</a></sup> Microsavings are designs to make savings products available for the poor, who make small deposits. <a href="/wiki/Mobile_banking" title="Mobile banking">Mobile banking</a> utilizes the wide availability of mobile phones to address the problem of the heavy regulation and costly maintenance of <a href="/wiki/Saving_account" class="mw-redirect" title="Saving account">saving accounts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-time.com_229-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time.com-229">[228]</a></sup> This usually involves a network of agents of mostly shopkeepers, instead of bank branches, would take deposits in cash and translate these onto a virtual account on customers' phones. Cash transfers can be done between phones and issued back in cash with a small commission, making <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a> safer.<sup id="cite_ref-safaricom_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-safaricom-230">[229]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wealth_concentration">Wealth concentration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Wealth concentration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">Economic inequality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wealth_concentration" title="Wealth concentration">Wealth concentration</a></div>
<p>Poverty can also be reduced as an improved economic policy is developed by the governing authorities to facilitate a more equitable distribution of the nation's wealth. <a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a> has called for an international movement to end extreme wealth concentration as a significant step towards ameliorating global poverty. The group stated that the $240 billion added to the fortunes of the world's richest billionaires in 2012 was enough to end extreme poverty four times over. Oxfam argues that the "concentration of resources in the hands of the top 1% depresses economic activity and makes life harder for everyone else – particularly those at the bottom of the economic ladder."<sup id="cite_ref-WP-20130120_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP-20130120-231">[230]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC-20130118_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-20130118-232">[231]</a></sup> It has been reported that only 1% of the world population controls 50% of the wealth today, and the other 99% is having access to the remaining 50% only, and the gap has sharply increased in the recent past.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[232]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Antonio_Ocampo" title="José Antonio Ocampo">José Antonio Ocampo</a>, professor at Columbia University and former finance minister of Colombia, and Magdalena Sepúlveda Carmona, former UN Special Rapporteur on Extreme Poverty and Human Rights, argue that global tax reform is integral to human development and fighting poverty, as corporate tax avoidance has disproportionately impacted those mired in poverty, noting that "the human impact is devastatingly real. When profits are shifted out, the tax revenues from those profits that could be available to fund healthcare, schools, water sanitation and other public goods vanish from the ledger, leaving women and men, boys and girls without pathways to a better future."<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[233]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Raghuram_Rajan" title="Raghuram Rajan">Raghuram G. Rajan</a>, governor of the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Bank_of_India" title="Reserve Bank of India">Reserve Bank of India</a>, former chief economist at the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and professor of finance at the <a href="/wiki/Booth_School_of_Business" title="Booth School of Business">University of Chicago Booth School of Business</a> has blamed the ever-widening gulf between the rich and the poor especially in the USA to be one of the main <i>Fault Lines</i> which caused the financial institutions to pump money into subprime mortgages – on political behest, as a palliative and not a remedy, for poverty – causing the <a href="/wiki/Subprime_mortgage_crisis" title="Subprime mortgage crisis">financial crisis of 2007 – 2009</a>. In Rajan's view the main cause of increasing gap between the high income and low income earners, was lack of equal access to high class education for the latter.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[234]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_solutions_to_poverty">Business solutions to poverty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Business solutions to poverty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bottom_of_the_pyramid" title="Bottom of the pyramid">Bottom of the pyramid</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fakirnibacha~2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Fakirnibacha~2.jpg/220px-Fakirnibacha~2.jpg" width="220" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/45/Fakirnibacha~2.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="303" data-file-height="320" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fakirnibacha~2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A poor child walks with one sandal.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Serving_the_poor_market">Serving the poor market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Serving the poor market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The concept of business serving the world's poorest four billion or so people has been popular since CK Prahalad introduced the idea through his book <i>Fortune at the Bottom of the Pyramid: Eradicating Poverty Through Profits</i> in 2004, among many business corporations and business schools.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[235]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[236]</a></sup> Kash Rangan, John Quelch, and other faculty members at the Global Poverty Project at <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Business_School" title="Harvard Business School">Harvard Business School</a> "believe that in pursuing its own self-interest in opening and expanding the BoP market, business can make a profit while serving the poorest of consumers and contributing to development."<sup id="cite_ref-hbswk.hbs.edu_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hbswk.hbs.edu-238">[237]</a></sup> According to Rangan "For business, the bulk of emerging markets worldwide is at the bottom of the pyramid so it makes good business sense—not a sense of do-gooding—to go after it.".<sup id="cite_ref-hbswk.hbs.edu_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hbswk.hbs.edu-238">[237]</a></sup></p>
<p>In their 2013 book, "The Business Solution to Poverty," Paul Polak and Mal Warwick directly addressed the criticism leveled against Prahalad’s concept.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[238]</a></sup> They noted that big business often failed to create products that actually met the needs and desires of the customers who lived at the bottom-of-the-pyramid. Their answer was that a business that wanted to success in that market had to spend time talking to and understanding those customers. Polak had previously promoted this approach in his previous book, "Out of Poverty," that described the work of <a href="/wiki/International_Development_Enterprises" title="International Development Enterprises">International Development Enterprises</a> (iDE), which he had formed in 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[239]</a></sup> Polak and Warwick provided practical advice: a product needed to affect at least a billion people (i.e., have universal appeal), it had to be able to be delivered to customers living where there wasn’t a FedEx office or even a road, and it had to be “radically affordable” to attract someone who earned less than $2 a day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Creating_entrepreneurs">Creating entrepreneurs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Creating entrepreneurs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rather than encouraging mutli-national businesses to meet the needs of the poor, some organizations such as iDE, the <a href="/wiki/World_Resources_Institute" title="World Resources Institute">World Resources Institute</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> began to focus on working directly with helping bottom-of-the-pyramid populations become local, small-scale entrepreneurs. Since so much of this population is engaged in agriculture, these NGOs have addressed market gaps that enable small-scale (i.e., plots less than 2 hectares) farmers to increase their production and find markets for their harvests. This is done by increasing the availability of farming equipment (e.g., pumps, tillers, seeders) and better quality seed and fertilizer, as well as expanding access for training in farming best practices (e.g., crop rotation).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticisms_of_this_approach">Criticisms of this approach</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Criticisms of this approach">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the view of Friedman <i>the social responsibility of business is to increase its profits</i> only,<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[240]</a></sup> thus, it needs to be examined whether business in BoP markets is capable of achieving the dual objective of <i>making a profit while serving the poorest of consumers and contributing to development</i>? Erik Simanis has reported that the model has a fatal flaw. According to Erik "Despite achieving healthy penetration rates of 5% to 10% in four test markets, for instance, Procter &amp; Gamble couldn’t generate a competitive return on its Pur water-purification powder after launching the product on a large scale in 2001...DuPont ran into similar problems with a venture piloted from 2006 to 2008 in Andhra Pradesh, India, by its subsidiary Solae, a global manufacturer of soy protein ... Because the high costs of doing business among the very poor demand a high contribution per transaction, companies must embrace the reality that high margins and price points aren’t just a top-of-the-pyramid phenomenon; they’re also a necessity for ensuring sustainable businesses at the bottom of the pyramid."<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[241]</a></sup> Marc Gunther states that "The bottom-of-the-pyramid (BOP) market leader, arguably, is Unilever ... Its signature BOP product is Pureit, a countertop water-purification system sold in India, Africa and Latin America. It's saving lives, but it's not making money for shareholders."<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[242]</a></sup> This leaves the ideal of <i>eradicating poverty through profits</i> or with a <i>good business sense—not a sense of do-gooding</i> rather questionable.</p>
<p>Others have noted that relying on BoP consumers to choose to purchase items that increase their incomes is naive. Poor consumers may spend their income disproportionately on events or goods and services that offer short-term benefits rather than invest in things that could change their lives in the long-term.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[243]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">Sustainable development</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming" title="Effects of global warming">Effects of global warming</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG/250px-Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG/375px-Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG/500px-Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Sewage_treatment" title="Sewage treatment">sewage treatment</a> plant that uses <a href="/wiki/Solar_energy" title="Solar energy">solar energy</a>, located at <a href="/wiki/Santuari_de_Lluc" title="Santuari de Lluc">Santuari de Lluc</a> monastery, Majorca.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A report published in 2013 by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, with support from the <a href="/wiki/Climate_%26_Development_Knowledge_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network">Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network</a>, found that climate change was likely to hinder future attempts to reduce poverty. The report presented the likely impacts of present day, 2&#160;°C and 4&#160;°C warming on agricultural production, water resources, coastal ecosystems and cities across Sub-Saharan Africa, South Asia and South East Asia. The impacts of a temperature rise of 2&#160;°C included: regular food shortages in Sub-Saharan Africa; shifting rain patterns in South Asia leaving some parts under water and others without enough water for power generation, irrigation or drinking; degradation and loss of reefs in South East Asia, resulting in reduced fish stocks; and coastal communities and cities more vulnerable to increasingly violent storms.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[244]</a></sup> In 2016, A UN report claimed that by 2030, an additional 122 million more people could be driven to extreme poverty because of climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[245]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to an Australian scientist Professor Frank Fenner, humans will not be able to survive the population explosion and “unbridled consumption,” and will become extinct, perhaps within a century, along with many other species. He believes the situation is irreversible, and it is too late because the effects we have had on Earth since industrialisation rivals any effects of ice ages or comet impacts.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[246]</a></sup> Harvard biologist E.O. Wilson calculated that Earth would lose half its higher life forms by 2100 if the current rate of human disruption continued.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[247]</a></sup> Many think that poverty is the cause of environmental degradation, while there are others who claim that rather the poor are the worst sufferers of environmental degradation caused by reckless exploitation of natural resources by the rich.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[248]</a></sup> A Delhi-based environment organisation, the Centre for Science and Environment, points out that if the poor world were to develop and consume in the same manner as the West to achieve the same living standards, “we would need two additional planet Earths to produce resources and absorb wastes.”, reports Anup Shah (2003). in his article <i>Poverty and the Environment</i> on Global Issues.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[249]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Voluntary_poverty">Voluntary poverty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Voluntary poverty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Simple_living" title="Simple living">Simple living</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_counsels" title="Evangelical counsels">Evangelical counsels</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg/220px-Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg" width="220" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg/330px-Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg/440px-Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg 2x" data-file-width="652" data-file-height="746" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
St. <a href="/wiki/Francis_of_Assisi" title="Francis of Assisi">Francis of Assisi</a> renounces his worldly goods in a painting attributed to <a href="/wiki/Giotto_di_Bondone" class="mw-redirect" title="Giotto di Bondone">Giotto di Bondone</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Among some individuals, poverty is considered a necessary or desirable condition, which must be embraced to reach certain spiritual, moral, or intellectual states. Poverty is often understood to be an essential element of <a href="/wiki/Nekkhamma" title="Nekkhamma">renunciation</a> in religions such as <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (only for monks, not for lay persons) and <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a>, whilst in Roman Catholicism it is one of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_counsels" title="Evangelical counsels">evangelical counsels</a>. The main aim of giving up things of the materialistic world is to withdraw oneself from sensual pleasures (as they are fake and temporary in some religions). This self-invited poverty (or giving up pleasures) is different from the one caused by economic imbalance.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Benedict_XVI" class="mw-redirect" title="Benedict XVI">Benedict XVI</a> distinguished "poverty <i>chosen</i>" (the poverty of spirit proposed by Jesus), and "poverty <i>to be fought</i>" (unjust and imposed poverty). He considered that the moderation implied in the former favors solidarity, and is a necessary condition so as to fight effectively to eradicate the abuse of the latter.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[250]</a></sup></p>
<p>As it was indicated above the reduction of poverty results from <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a>, but also can result from <a href="/wiki/Solidarity" title="Solidarity">solidarity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[251]</a></sup></p>

In 2004, 1.1 billion people lived in extreme poverty on less than a dollar a day.</span></li>

University of Chicago Press. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-226-03365-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-226-03365-5">978-0-226-03365-5</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APoverty&amp;rft.au=Babb%2C+Sarah&amp;rft.btitle=Behind+the+Development+Banks%3A+Washington+Politics%2C+World+Poverty%2C+and+the+Wealth+of+Nations&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-226-03365-5&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Chicago+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>

<li>Brady, David "Rethinking the Sociological Measurement of Poverty" <i>Social Forces</i> 81#3 2003, pp.&#160;715–751 Online in Project Muse. <small>Abstract: Reviews shortcomings of the official U.S. measure; examines several theoretical and methodological advances in poverty measurement. Argues that ideal measures of poverty should: (1) measure comparative historical variation effectively; (2) be relative rather than absolute; (3) conceptualize poverty as social exclusion; (4) assess the impact of taxes, transfers, and state benefits; and (5) integrate the depth of poverty and the inequality among the poor. Next, this article evaluates sociological studies published since 1990 for their consideration of these criteria. This article advocates for three alternative poverty indices: the interval measure, the ordinal measure, and the sum of ordinals measure. Finally, using the <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_Income_Study" title="Luxembourg Income Study">Luxembourg Income Study</a>, it examines the empirical patterns with these three measures, across advanced capitalist democracies from 1967 to 1997. Estimates of these poverty indices are made available.</small></li>

<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://hdl.handle.net/10822/552568">Reducing Global Poverty</a> from the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://repository.library.georgetown.edu/handle/10822/552494">Dean Peter Krogh Foreign Affairs Digital Archives</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ourworldindata.org/data/growth-and-distribution-of-prosperity/world-poverty/">Data visualizations of the long-run development of poverty and list of data sources on poverty</a> on 'Our World in Data'.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.isdb.org/irj/portal/anonymous">Islamic Development Bank</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.lisproject.org/">Luxembourg Income Study</a> Contains a wealth of data on income inequality and poverty, and hundreds of its sponsored research papers using this data.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.oecd.org/">Organization for Economic Cooperation and Development</a> Contains reports on economic development as well as relations between rich and poor nations.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ophi.qeh.ox.ac.uk/">OPHI</a> <a href="/wiki/Oxford_Poverty_%26_Human_Development_Initiative" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford Poverty &amp; Human Development Initiative">Oxford Poverty &amp; Human Development Initiative</a> (OPHI)] Research to advance the human development approach to poverty reduction.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.transparency.org/">Transparency International</a> Tracks issues of government and corporate corruption around the world.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.un.org/english">United Nations</a> Hundreds of free reports related to economic development and standards of living in countries around the world, such as the annual <i>Human Development Report.</i></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.usaid.gov/">U.S. Agency for International Development</a> USAID is the primary U.S. government agency with the mission for aid to developing countries.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.worldbank.org/">World Bank</a> Contains hundreds of reports which can be downloaded for free, such as the annual <i>World Development Report.</i></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.wfp.org/">World Food Program</a> Associated with the United Nations, the World Food Program compiles hundreds of reports on hunger and food security around the world.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.whypoverty.net/">Why poverty</a> Documentary films about poverty broadcast on television around the world in November 2012, then will be available online.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.oxfam.org/en/pressroom/pressrelease/2013-01-19/annual-income-richest-100-people-enough-end-global-poverty-four-times">Annual income of richest 100 people enough to end global poverty four times over</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Oxfam_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxfam International">Oxfam International</a>,</i> 19 January 2013.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=xxZi6pe2DgQC&amp;pg=PA15&amp;dq=poverty+belgium+1975&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ei=Z3-dU8DKD8G-O8XugcgH&amp;ved=0CCkQ6AEwAg#v=onepage&amp;q=poverty%20belgium%201975&amp;f=false">Contains estimates on the number of people living in poverty in selected countries from 1973 to 1985</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/wonkblog/wp/2015/01/14/this-powerful-reddit-thread-reveals-how-the-poor-get-by-in-america/?tid=sm_fb">This powerful Reddit thread reveals how the poor get by in America</a> (January 2015), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://hdr.undp.org/sites/default/files/hdr14-summary-en.pdf">Summary of Human Development Report 2014</a>, by the <i><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a></i></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.truthdig.com/eartotheground/item/22_billion_people_are_poor_20140723">2.2 Billion People Are Poor</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Truthdig" title="Truthdig">Truthdig</a>,</i> 23 July 2014.</li>
